## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillations and dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form for (non)linear harmonic oscillators. Common models combine a restoring force term (often nonlinear in x), damping (often proportional or nonlinear in v), and optional external/parametric forcing terms that depend on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hookean restoring force, small oscillations)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven linear oscillator (sine form): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Duffing oscillator (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity)
- Duffing with drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos/bi-stability regimes)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle model: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (nonlinear restoring from gravity torque)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * v**2) * v (velocity-dependent energy injection/removal)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag-dominated dissipation)
- Nonlinear stiffness with quintic term: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear spring)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu-type)
- Potential-force form (gradient dynamics with damping): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) - c2 * v (dv_dt = -dU/dx - damping, with U ~ x^2 + x^4)
- Mixed nonlinear coupling: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent damping / internal friction surrogate)
- External forcing with nonlinear stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear restoring plus periodic drive)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: if the oscillator is symmetric about x=0, dv_dt often contains odd functions of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3, -c*sin(x)) and avoids even-only stiffness terms.
- Energy dissipation: terms proportional to -v or -v*Abs(v) indicate monotone energy loss per cycle; the presence/absence of such terms strongly affects whether trajectories spiral toward equilibrium.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: adding stiffness nonlinearities (e.g., -c*x**3, -c*x**5) produces frequency that changes with amplitude (hardening/softening behavior).
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: damping that changes sign with state (e.g., (1-c*x**2)*v or (1-c*v**2)*v) suggests stable oscillations without external forcing.
- Periodic driving: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms indicate an external actuator; responses commonly show resonance/entrainment when c matches the natural frequency scale from the x-term.
- Parametric resonance: time-multiplying stiffness (-(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates modulation of system parameters; instability tongues and subharmonic responses are typical.
- Large-angle pendulum signature: sin(x) restoring (instead of x) points to rotational/angle coordinates and predicts period increase with amplitude.
- Nonlinear damping via x-v coupling: terms like -c*x**2*v model internal friction where dissipation depends on displacement amplitude as well as velocity.
- Conservative vs nonconservative split: models often decompose as dv_dt = f(x,t) + g(x,v,t) where f is derived from a potential (depends on x,t) and g contains damping/drive (depends on v and/or t).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO32)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):
\[
-0.0907042821530562\,v^3\;-\;0.594472842575296\,v\,e^{-|v|}\;-\;2.9429090494833\,x^3\;+\;0.56911073046847\,\sin(t)
\]
Key structural requirements:
- Has a **non-polynomial** damping term \(v e^{-|v|}\) (depends on \(|v|\) inside an exponential).
- Has **only** \(v^3\), \(x^3\), and a pure sinusoid in \(t\); **no** rational-in-\(t\) terms like \(1/(c+t)\) or \(x/(c+t)\); **no** constant offsets; **no** linear \(v\) or \(v|v|\) terms.
- Trig: candidate’s \(c\cos(t+\phi)\) can match \(A\sin t\) by choosing \(\phi=\pi/2\) and \(c=-A\) (since \(\cos(t+\pi/2)=-\sin t\)).

Now check candidates: all candidates are built from combinations of
- polynomials in \(v\): \(v, v^3, v|v|, v|v|^2\) (note \(v|v|^2 = v^3\)),
- polynomials in \(x\): \(x^3\),
- trig: \(\cos(t+\text{phase})\),
- and sometimes rational terms in \(t\): \(1/(c+t)\), \(x/(c+t)\), etc.

None of these building blocks can produce the GT’s essential term \(v e^{-|v|}\). There is no exponential of \(|v|\) anywhere in any candidate, so **no choice of constants** can make a purely algebraic expression in \(v\) equal to \(v e^{-|v|}\) for all real \(v\). (They could coincide at finitely many points, but not as functions on a domain where \(v\) varies and can be negative.)

Still, for completeness, I’ll also note other mismatches that would need to be “zeroed out” even if the exponential issue didn’t exist.

### Candidates 1–4
Contain \(v^3\), \(v|v|\), \(x^3\), \(\cos(t+\cdot)\), plus extra terms like \(v\), \(x/(c+t)\), \(1/(c+t)\), and/or duplicated \(v\) terms.
- You can set coefficients of \(v\), \(x/(c+t)\), \(1/(c+t)\) to 0 to remove them, and phase-shift cosine to match \(\sin t\).
- But they still only have polynomial/absolute-value algebraic damping (\(v|v|\), \(v^3\)), **not** \(v e^{-|v|}\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidate 5
Has \(v^3\), \(x^3\), \(\cos(t+\cdot)\), \(v\), rational-in-\(t\) terms, and \(v|v|\) plus an extra fixed \(v|v|\) term.
- Rational terms can be zeroed by setting their coefficients to 0.
- But again no \(v e^{-|v|}\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 6–8
Include constants and/or linear \(v\) terms and \(v|v|\), plus possible rational terms.
- Constants/linear terms can be set to 0.
- Still no exponential damping term.
⇒ Not match.

### Candidate 9
Has \(x/(c_7 t+c_8)\) and \(1/(c_8+t)\) plus a trailing \(+v\).
- Those can’t be made identically absent unless their coefficients are 0 (possible), and the trailing \(+v\) cannot be removed (coefficient is 1).
- Even ignoring that, no \(v e^{-|v|}\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidate 10
Can zero rational terms; trig can phase shift; polynomial terms adjustable.
- Missing \(v e^{-|v|}\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 11–12
Have extra linear \(v\) terms and/or rational terms; 12 also has unavoidable \(+v\) and \(+1/(c_7+t)\) (the latter has fixed coefficient 1).
- Unavoidable terms already break equivalence.
- Also no \(v e^{-|v|}\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 13–18
Various rational-in-\(t\) terms; some have unavoidable \(+v\) or \(+1/(c_7+t)\).
- Any unavoidable \(+v\) or \(+1/(c_7+t)\) immediately prevents matching GT.
- Regardless, none has \(v e^{-|v|}\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 19–22
Include constants and/or rational terms and sometimes an extra \(+v\).
- If \(+v\) appears with fixed coefficient 1 (e.g., 21 has “+ v”), it cannot be removed.
- Even when removable, still no \(v e^{-|v|}\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 23–32
Contain an added constant \(c_8\) in some, or rational terms, or an unavoidable \(+v\) in some.
- Constants/rational terms can often be zeroed if they have coefficients, but any explicit “+ v” cannot.
- None contains \(v e^{-|v|}\).
⇒ Not match.

### Candidates 33–50
These are sums of polynomial terms in \(v\) (including multiple \(v^3\) terms), \(v|v|\), constants, \(x^3\) (sometimes duplicated), and \(\cos(t+\cdot)\).
- Duplicated \(v^3\) or \(x^3\) can be combined by choosing coefficients appropriately.
- Cosine can be phase-shifted to match sine.
- Constants and linear \(v\) terms can be set to 0 **only when they have free coefficients**; but some forms include extra fixed terms like “+ v**3” (candidate 43) or “+ x**3” (candidate 48) which are not removable.
- Crucially: still **no** \(v e^{-|v|}\) term in any of them.
⇒ Not match.

### Core impossibility argument (applies to all 1–50)
Every candidate is an algebraic combination of \(v\), \(|v|\), \(x\), \(t\), trig in \(t\), and rational functions of \(t\). After choosing constants and removing optional terms, the \(v\)-dependence remains a finite combination of polynomial-type terms (possibly with \(|v|\) factors), i.e., piecewise-polynomial in \(v\). The GT contains \(v e^{-|v|}\), which is not piecewise-polynomial and cannot be represented exactly by any finite polynomial/absolute-value expression for all real \(v\). Therefore no candidate can be made identical to GT on the oscillator’s domain.

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v - omega0**c1*x**c2

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0907*v³ - 0.5945*v*exp(-|v|) - 2.9429*x³ + 0.5691*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v³`
2. `v*exp(-|v|)` — this is a specific nonlinear function
3. `x³`
4. `sin(t)` (equivalently `cos(t + c)` with appropriate phase shift)

The critical term is `v*exp(-|v|)`. This is NOT equivalent to:
- `v*|v|` (which equals `v²*sign(v)`)
- `v*|v|²` (which equals `v³`)
- Any polynomial in `v`
- Any combination of `v*|v|` and `v³`

Let me verify: `v*exp(-|v|)` is a function that decays exponentially for large |v|, while `v*|v|` grows quadratically. These are fundamentally different basis functions and cannot be made equivalent by any choice of constants.

**Key observation:** Every single candidate uses combinations of:
- `v³`
- `v*|v|` (or `v*|v|²` = `v³`)
- `x³`
- `cos(c + t)` ≡ `sin(t)` with phase shift
- `v` (linear)
- Various terms with `1/(c + t)` or `x/(c + t)`
- Constants

None of them contain `exp(-|v|)` or any exponential function of `v`.

The GT requires `v*exp(-|v|)` with coefficient `-0.5945`, which is not negligible. Since `v*exp(-|v|)` cannot be expressed as any finite combination of polynomials in `v`, `v*|v|`, rational functions of `t`, `x³`, or trigonometric functions, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me double-check candidates with `v*|v|²`: Note that `v*|v|² = v*v² = v³` for all real `v`, so this just adds to the `v³` term. This doesn't help create `v*exp(-|v|)`.

For candidates with both `v*|v|` and `v³`: The function `v*|v|` behaves as `v²` for `v>0` and `-v²` for `v<0`, while `v*exp(-|v|)` decays exponentially. No linear combination of `v*|v|`, `v³`, and `v` can equal `v*exp(-|v|)` for all `v`.

Therefore, every candidate is a **[NO MATCH]**.
